Because unlike writing an OS or vaccine delivery system, where failure modes are predictable and isolated, in cross-chain MEV your entire position depends on the weakest link in a chain of independent networks, oracles, bridges, and smart contracts.\n\nSo if I were to build a piece of this system ‚Äî not to speculate, but to understand ‚Äî I‚Äôd start with the smallest *verifiable* component: **on-chain event anomaly detection**.\n\nNot arbitrage. Not execution. **Detection**.\n\nBecause before you can act on an opportunity across chains, you must first know what‚Äôs normal ‚Äî so you can identify what‚Äôs exploitable.\n\nHere‚Äôs how I‚Äôd implement it:\n\n```python\nimport numpy as np\nfrom collections import deque\n\nclass OnChainAnomalyDetector:\n    def __init__(self, window_size=100):\n        self.window = deque(maxlen=window_size)\n        self.threshold = 2.0  # Standard deviations\n\n    def update(self, value):\n        if value <= 0:\n            return False  # Skip invalid values (e.g., gas=0)\n        self.window.append(value)\n        return len(self.window) == self.window.maxlen\n\n    def is_anomalous(self, value):\n        if not self.update(value):\n            return False\n\n        mean = np.mean(self.window)\n        std = np.std(self.window)\n        z_score = abs(value - mean) / (std + 1e-6)\n\n        return z_score > self.threshold\n\n# Usage example:\ndetector = OnChainAnomalyDetector(window_size=50)\n\nfor tx in mempool_stream:\n    gas_price = tx['gas_price']\n    if detector.is_anomalous(gas_price):\n        print(f\"Anomaly detected: {gas_price} gwei (potential frontrun or spam)\")\n```\n\nThis is the foundation: a stateful monitor that learns baseline behavior (e.g., swap size, gas spikes, pool liquidity changes) on any chain. Only once you can reliably detect anomalies do you even have a signal worth acting on.\n\nNo leverage. No flash loans.
